<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_service">In service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: In service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Warrior_(2011)" title="Rainbow Warrior (2011)">Rainbow Warrior</a></i> is the third vessel to bear the name. Launched in 2011, it is sometimes referred to as <i>Rainbow Warrior III</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-COMM_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COMM-157">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Arctic_Sunrise" title="MV Arctic Sunrise">MV <i>Arctic Sunrise</i></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Esperanza" title="MV Esperanza">MV <i>Esperanza</i></a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Previously_in_service">Previously in service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Previously in service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Rainbow_Warrior">First <i>Rainbow Warrior</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: First Rainbow Warrior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Warrior_(1955)" title="Rainbow Warrior (1955)"><i>Rainbow Warrior</i> (1955)</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_Rainbow_Warrior" title="Sinking of the Rainbow Warrior">Sinking of the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i></a></div>
<p>In 1978, Greenpeace launched the original <i><a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Warrior_(1955)" title="Rainbow Warrior (1955)">Rainbow Warrior</a></i>, a 40-metre (130&#160;ft), former fishing <a href="/wiki/Commercial_trawler" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial trawler">trawler</a> named for the book <i><a href="/wiki/Legend_of_the_Rainbow_Warriors" title="Legend of the Rainbow Warriors">Warriors of the Rainbow</a></i>, which inspired early activist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hunter_(journalist)" title="Robert Hunter (journalist)">Robert Hunter</a> on the first voyage to Amchitka. Greenpeace purchased the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i> (originally launched as the <i>Sir William Hardy</i> in 1955) at a cost of £40,000. Volunteers restored and refitted it over a period of four months. First deployed to disrupt the hunt of the <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Icelandic</a> whaling fleet, the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i> would quickly become a mainstay of Greenpeace campaigns. Between 1978 and 1985, crew members also engaged in direct action against the ocean-dumping of toxic and radioactive waste, the <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seal</a> hunt in <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> and nuclear testing in the Pacific. In May 1985, the vessel was instrumental for 'Operation Exodus', the evacuation of about 300 <a href="/wiki/Rongelap_Atoll" title="Rongelap Atoll">Rongelap Atoll</a> islanders whose home had been contaminated with nuclear fallout from a US nuclear test two decades ago which had never been cleaned up and was still having severe health effects on the locals.<sup id="cite_ref-GREEN_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GREEN-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later in 1985 the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i> was to lead a flotilla of protest vessels into the waters surrounding <a href="/wiki/Moruroa" title="Moruroa">Moruroa</a> atoll, site of French nuclear testing. The <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_Rainbow_Warrior" title="Sinking of the Rainbow Warrior">sinking of the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i></a> occurred when the <a href="/wiki/French_government" class="mw-redirect" title="French government">French government</a> secretly bombed the ship in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> harbour on orders from <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">François Mitterrand</a> himself. This killed Dutch freelance photographer <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pereira" title="Fernando Pereira">Fernando Pereira</a>, who thought it was safe to enter the boat to get his photographic material after a first small explosion, but drowned as a result of a second, larger explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The attack was a public relations disaster for France after it was quickly exposed by the New Zealand police. The French Government in 1987 agreed to pay New Zealand compensation of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_dollar" title="New Zealand dollar">NZ$</a>13 million and formally apologised for the bombing. The French Government also paid <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">₣</a>2.3 million compensation to the family of the photographer. Later, in 2001, when the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Cetacean_Research" title="Institute of Cetacean Research">Institute of Cetacean Research</a> of Japan called Greenpeace "<a href="/wiki/Ecoterrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecoterrorism">eco-terrorists</a>", Gert Leipold, then Executive Director of Greenpeace, detested the claim, saying "calling non violent protest terrorism insults those who were injured or killed in the attacks of real terrorists, including Fernando Pereira, killed by State terrorism in the 1985 attack on the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Rainbow_Warrior">Second <i>Rainbow Warrior</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Second Rainbow Warrior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Warrior_(1957)" title="Rainbow Warrior (1957)"><i>Rainbow Warrior</i> (1957)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg/200px-Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg/300px-Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg/400px-Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greenpeace_Rainbow_Warrior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Greenpeace's second <i><a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Warrior_(1989)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainbow Warrior (1989)">Rainbow Warrior</a></i> ship arrives in <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2007_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2007 United Nations Climate Change Conference">2007 UN climate conference</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1989 Greenpeace commissioned a replacement Rainbow Warrior vessel, sometimes referred to as <i>Rainbow Warrior II</i>. It retired from service on 16 August 2011, to be replaced by the third generation vessel. In 2005 the <i>Rainbow Warrior II</i> ran aground on and damaged the <a href="/wiki/Tubbataha_Reef" title="Tubbataha Reef">Tubbataha Reef</a> in the Philippines while inspecting the reef for <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a>. Greenpeace was fined <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>7,000 for damaging the reef and agreed to pay the fine saying they felt responsible for the damage, although Greenpeace stated that the Philippines government had given it outdated charts. The park manager of Tubbataha appreciated the quick action Greenpeace took to assess the damage to the reef.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Sirius" title="MV Sirius">MV <i>Sirius</i></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Solo" title="MV Solo">MV <i>Solo</i></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Greenpeace" title="MV Greenpeace">MV <i>Greenpeace</i></a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MV_Gondwana" title="MV Gondwana">MV <i>Gondwana</i></a></li>
<li><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beluga_(Schiff)" class="extiw" title="de:Beluga (Schiff)">MV <i>Beluga</i></a> (in German)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_and_responses_to_Greenpeace_activities">Reactions and responses to Greenpeace activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Reactions and responses to Greenpeace activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lawsuits have been filed against Greenpeace for lost profits,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> reputation damage<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Sailormongering" title="Sailormongering">sailormongering</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> In 2004 it was revealed that the Australian government was willing to offer a subsidy to <a href="/wiki/Southern_Pacific_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Pacific Petroleum">Southern Pacific Petroleum</a> on the condition that the oil company would take legal action against Greenpeace, which had campaigned against the <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Oil_Shale_Project" title="Stuart Oil Shale Project">Stuart Oil Shale Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some corporations, such as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_de_France" title="Électricité de France">Électricité de France</a> have reacted to Greenpeace campaigns by spying on Greenpeace activities and infiltrating Greenpeace offices.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Greenpeace activists have also been targets of phone tapping, death threats, violence<sup id="cite_ref-Timmer_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timmer-37">[37]</a></sup> and even <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a> in the case of the bombing of the <i>Rainbow Warrior</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robie_D_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robie_D-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Greenpeace" title="Criticism of Greenpeace">Criticism of Greenpeace</a></div>
<p>Canadian ecologist <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Moore_(environmentalist)" title="Patrick Moore (environmentalist)">Patrick Moore</a>, an early Greenpeace member, left the organization in 1986 when it, according to Moore, decided to support a universal ban on <a href="/wiki/Chlorine" title="Chlorine">chlorine</a><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> in drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-moore_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore-19">[19]</a></sup> Moore has argued that Greenpeace today is motivated by politics rather than science and that none of his "fellow directors had any formal science education".<sup id="cite_ref-moore_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore-19">[19]</a></sup> Bruce Cox, Director of Greenpeace Canada, responded that Greenpeace has never demanded a universal chlorine ban and that Greenpeace does not oppose use of chlorine in drinking water or in pharmaceutical uses, adding that "Mr. Moore is alone in his recollection of a fight over chlorine and/or use of science as his reason for leaving Greenpeace."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Watson" title="Paul Watson">Paul Watson</a>, an early member of Greenpeace has said that Moore "uses his status as a so-called co-founder of Greenpeace to give credibility to his accusations. I am also a co-founder of Greenpeace and I have known Patrick Moore for 35 years.[...] Moore makes accusations that have no basis in fact".<sup id="cite_ref-examiner_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-examiner-172">[172]</a></sup> More recently Moore has been particularly critical of Greenpeace's stance on <a href="/wiki/Golden_rice" title="Golden rice">golden rice</a>, an issue where Moore has been joined by other environmentalists such as <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lynas" title="Mark Lynas">Mark Lynas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> claiming that Greenpeace has "waged a campaign of misinformation, trashed the scientists who are working to bring Golden Rice to the people who need it, and supported the violent destruction of Golden Rice field trials."<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Moore_(environmentalist)" title="Patrick Moore (environmentalist)">Patrick Moore</a> also reversed his position on <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> in 1976,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> first opposing it and now supporting it.<sup id="cite_ref-wapo_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> In Australian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age" title="The Age">The Age</a></i>, he writes "Greenpeace is wrong—we must consider nuclear power".<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> He argues that any realistic plan to reduce reliance on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> or <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions need increased use of nuclear energy.<sup id="cite_ref-wapo_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo-176">[176]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phil_Radford" title="Phil Radford">Phil Radford</a>, Executive Director of Greenpeace US responded that nuclear energy is too risky, takes too long to build to address <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, and claims that most countries, including the U.S., could shift to nearly 100% <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> while phasing out nuclear power by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>A French journalist under the pen name Olivier Vermont wrote in his book <i>La Face cachée de Greenpeace</i> ("The Hidden Face of Greenpeace") that he had joined Greenpeace France and had worked there as a secretary. According to Vermont he found misconduct, and continued to find it, from Amsterdam to the International office. Vermont said he found classified documents<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> according to which half of the organization's €180 million revenue was used for the organization's salaries and structure. He also accused Greenpeace of having unofficial agreements with polluting companies where the companies paid Greenpeace to keep them from attacking the company's image.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Animal protection magazine <i>Animal People</i> reported in March 1997 that Greenpeace France and Greenpeace International had sued Olivier Vermont and his publisher Albin Michel for issuing "defamatory statements, untruths, distortions of the facts and absurd allegations".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmos_(magazine)" title="Cosmos (magazine)">Cosmos</a></i>, journalist <a href="/wiki/Wilson_da_Silva" title="Wilson da Silva">Wilson da Silva</a> reacted to Greenpeace's destruction of a genetically modified wheat crop in <a href="/wiki/Ginninderra" title="Ginninderra">Ginninderra</a> as another sign that the organization has "lost its way" and had degenerated into a "sad, dogmatic, reactionary phalanx of anti-science zealots who care not for evidence, but for publicity".<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press_release_blunder">Press release blunder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Press release blunder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Philadelphia, in 2006, Greenpeace issued a press release that said "In the twenty years since the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl</a> tragedy, the world's worst nuclear accident, there have been nearly [FILL IN ALARMIST AND ARMAGEDDONIST FACTOID HERE]". The final report warned of plane crashes and reactor meltdowns.<sup id="cite_ref-wpkidding_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpkidding-186">[186]</a></sup> According to a Greenpeace spokesman, the memo was a joke that was accidentally released.<sup id="cite_ref-wpkidding_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpkidding-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brent_Spar_tanker">Brent Spar tanker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Brent Spar tanker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Research published in natural science journal <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> accused Greenpeace of not caring for facts, when it criticized the dumping of the <a href="/wiki/Brent_Spar" title="Brent Spar">Brent Spar</a> tanker, and accused the group of exaggerating the volume of oil that was stored in the tanker.<sup id="cite_ref-nature_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature-187">[187]</a></sup> Greenpeace had claimed that the tanker contained 5,500 tonnes of crude oil, while Shell estimated it only contained 50 tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-iaea_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-188">[188]</a></sup> In fact, the measurements had been made under duress during a protest occupation of the platform, since Shell had refused permission. Greenpeace was under attack by water cannons and the like.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> In fact, BBC issued an apology to Greenpeace for having reported that the NGO lied.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shell UK took three years to evaluate disposal option and concluded that the disposal of the tanker in the deep ocean was the "<a href="/wiki/Best_Practicable_Environmental_Option" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Practicable Environmental Option">Best Practicable Environmental Option</a>" (BPEO), an option which gained some support within some portion of the scientific community, as it was found by some to be of "negligible" environmental impact.<sup id="cite_ref-iaea_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-188">[188]</a></sup> British government and Oslo and Paris Commissions (OSPAR) accepted the solution.<sup id="cite_ref-iaea_188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>The resulting NGO campaign against Shell's proposals included letters, boycotts which even escalated to vandalism in Germany, and lobbying at intergovernmental conferences. Binding moratoriums supporting Greenpeace's, ecosystem protection, and the precautionary principle position were issued in more than one intergovernmental meeting, and at the 1998 OSPAR Convention, WWF presented a study of toxic effects on deep sea ecosystems. The meeting confirmed a general prohibition on ocean dumping.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Shell had transported the rig to the dumping site, but in the last hours canceled the operation and announced that it had failed in communicating its plans sufficiently to the public, admitting they had underestimated the strength of public opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-iaea_188-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-188">[188]</a></sup> In January, 1998, Shell issued a new BPEO indicating recycling the rig as a quay in Norway.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, the <a href="/wiki/Brent_Spar" title="Brent Spar">Brent Spar</a> container was decommissioned and one side issue that emerged was that the legs of the structure were found to contain cold-water coral species (<i>Lophelia pertusa</i>). As a result, the possibility was suggested of keeping the legs of such platforms on the sea bed in future, to serve as habitat.<sup id="cite_ref-iaea_188-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaea-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> A Greenpeace representative opposed the suggestion, citing the fact that the reefs formed by the coral are at risk, not the coral itself, and that such a move would not promote development of such reefs, and expose coral species to toxic substances found in oil.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pascal_Husting_commute">Pascal Husting commute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Pascal Husting commute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013 reports noted that Pascal Husting, the director of Greenpeace International's "international programme" was commuting 250 miles via plane, despite Greenpeace's activism to reduce air travel due to carbon footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Greenpeace has said "the growth in aviation is ruining our chances of stopping dangerous climate change".<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> After a "public uproar" Greenpeace announced that Husting would commute via train in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nazca_Lines">Nazca Lines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Nazca Lines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2014, Greenpeace activists damaged rock related to the <a href="/wiki/Nazca_Lines" title="Nazca Lines">Nazca Lines</a> in Peru while setting up a banner within the lines of one of the famed geoglyphs, and there were concerns that the harm might be irreparable. The activists damaged an area around the hummingbird by walking near the glyph without regulation footwear. Access to the area around the lines is strictly prohibited and<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_Nazca_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_Nazca-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt_nazca_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_nazca-203">[203]</a></sup> special shoes must be worn to avoid damaging the <a href="/wiki/UN_World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="UN World Heritage">UN World Heritage</a> site. Greenpeace claimed the activists were "absolutely careful to protect the Nazca lines,"<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> but this is contradicted by video and photographs showing the activists wearing conventional shoes (not special protective shoes) while walking on the site.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Greenpeace has apologized to the Peruvian people,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> but Loise Jamie Castillo, Peru's Vice Minister of Cultural Heritage called the apology "a joke", because Greenpeace refused to identify the vandals or accept responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Culture Minister Diana Álvarez-Calderón said that evidence gathered during an investigation by the government will be used as part of a legal suit against Greenpeace. "The damage done is irreparable and the apologies offered by the environmental group aren't enough," she said at a news conference.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_Nazca_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_Nazca-27">[27]</a></sup> By January, 2015, Greenpeace had presented statements of the four members of the NGO involved in the action.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti_Whaling_Campaign_in_Norway_in_the_1990s">Anti Whaling Campaign in Norway in the 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Anti Whaling Campaign in Norway in the 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1990s Greenpeace conducted many anti-whaling expeditions in Norway. The criticism was that Greenpeace only campaigned against whales to gain economic donations from the US economy, and it had little to do with saving the environment. For example, shark hunting is a much bigger problem for the environment, but since sharks are hated they're not a big money maker in the US. Greenpeace have always rejected this claim. However, in Norwegian Newspaper Dagbladet on 11 April 2015 <a href="/wiki/Kumi_Naidoo" title="Kumi Naidoo">Kumi Naidoo</a> admitted that the anti-whale campaign was a "miscalculation".<sup id="cite_ref-m.db.no_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m.db.no-210">[210]</a></sup> Greenpeace holds that whaling was only resumed by Norway after the IWC ban because of political election motives, and faces many explicit hurdles, including decreased demand in Japan and toxic chemical contamination.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_letter_from_Nobel_laureates">Open letter from Nobel laureates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Open letter from Nobel laureates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2016, 107 Nobel laureates signed an open letter<sup id="cite_ref-:0_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21">[21]</a></sup> urging Greenpeace to end its opposition to genetically modified organisms (GMOs).<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> The letter stated: "We urge Greenpeace and its supporters to re-examine the experience of farmers and consumers worldwide with crops and foods improved through biotechnology, recognize the findings of authoritative scientific bodies and regulatory agencies, and abandon their campaign against "GMOs" in general and Golden Rice in particular. Scientific and regulatory agencies around the world have repeatedly and consistently found crops and foods improved through biotechnology to be as safe as, if not safer than those derived from any other method of production. There has never been a single confirmed case of a negative health outcome for humans or animals from their consumption. Their environmental impacts have been shown repeatedly to be less damaging to the environment, and a boon to global biodiversity." The Nobel laureates also called upon governments of the world to "do everything in their power to oppose Greenpeace's actions and accelerate the access of farmers to all the tools of modern biology, especially seeds improved through biotechnology." The letter goes on to say that "Opposition based on emotion and dogma contradicted by data must be stopped."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21">[21]</a></sup> Greenpeace responded stating that "Accusations that anyone is blocking genetically engineered 'Golden' rice are false" and that they support "...investing in climate-resilient ecological agriculture and empowering farmers to access a balanced and nutritious diet, rather than pouring money down the drain for GE 'Golden' rice."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Nobel laureate letter has been itself subject to scrutiny, since the claims are unfounded. "Golden Rice" has not even been successfully brought to market, or even patented in the country where it is being tested. As such, no anti-GMO protesters have played any role in the GMO product's so far unsuccessful development. Moreover, the letter itself is structured in such a way that it uses many adjectives and extreme accusations without any substantiating references. It has been described as more similar to a work of biotech industry propaganda than a product of Nobel scientists.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_offices">Regional offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Regional offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_Aotearoa_New_Zealand">Greenpeace Aotearoa New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Greenpeace Aotearoa New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_Aotearoa_New_Zealand" title="Greenpeace Aotearoa New Zealand">Greenpeace Aotearoa New Zealand</a></div>
<p>Greenpeace Aotearoa New Zealand was founded in 1974, two years after the original Greenpeace, and is one of New Zealand's largest environmental organizations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_Australia_Pacific">Greenpeace Australia Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Greenpeace Australia Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_Australia_Pacific" title="Greenpeace Australia Pacific">Greenpeace Australia Pacific</a></div>
<p>Greenpeace Australia commenced operation in the 1970s. In early 1998 Greenpeace <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and Greenpeace Pacific teamed up to become Greenpeace Australia Pacific (GPAP), one of the region's largest environmental organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_Chile">Greenpeace Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Greenpeace Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Chile, the organization is affiliated as "Greenpeace Chile" was founded in 1981 and is a government recognized NGO there.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_East_Asia">Greenpeace East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Greenpeace East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_East_Asia" title="Greenpeace East Asia">Greenpeace East Asia</a></div>
<p>Greenpeace East Asia's first office was opened in Hong Kong in 1997. Greenpeace East Asia now campaigns in Hong Kong, Mainland China, Taiwan and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-greenpeaceeastasia_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenpeaceeastasia-216">[216]</a></sup> This branch also occasionally works with local education institutions, including Geography Society of <a href="/wiki/PLK_Vicwood_KT_Chong_Sixth_Form_College" title="PLK Vicwood KT Chong Sixth Form College">PLK Vicwood KT Chong Sixth Form College</a> between 2008 and 2009.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_India">Greenpeace India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Greenpeace India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_India" title="Greenpeace India">Greenpeace India</a></div>
<p>Greenpeace India has been working on various issues related to the environment since 2001. Their work in India is focused on four broad campaigns; Stop Climate Change, Sustainable Agriculture, Defending Our Oceans, and Nuclear.</p>
<p>In June-2014, Indian Intelligence Bureau in an internal report to Prime Minister's Office accused Greenpeace and other lobby groups of hurting economic progress by campaigning against power projects, mining and genetically modified food.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 9, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Home_Affairs_(India)" title="Ministry of Home Affairs (India)">The Union Home Ministry</a> blocked all the bank accounts of Greenpeace India on allegations of illegal opening and non disclosure of bank accounts to income tax authorities and financial mishandling of foreign donations.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> The organisation has also received a notice from the ministry.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> Later in May 2015, the Delhi High Court provided interim relief to open two of its domestic accounts to allow regular operations of the organisations but the money frozen by government was not allowed to be used pending further trial.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2015 following a revelation by an ex-employee in web forum<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> about repeated sexual harassment and rape at Greenpeace India and subsequent harassment for complaints, multiple women employees of Greenpeace India has come out talking about similar incidents of sexual harassment, bullying and rape at Greenpeace India. The women in her post alleged that the organisation only provided an apology e-mail and did not initiate any action against the alleged offender. The organisation was accused of protecting the offenders.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Following the accusations, Greenpeace India Executive Director, Samit Aich stepped down following an internal review. The board accepted his resignation, soon after Divya Raghunandan then Programme Director also resigned from her post and quit Greenpeace India.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 6, 2015, Government of India ordered de-registration of Greenpeace India citing financial fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Greenpeace India's interim Executive Director, Vinuta Gopal filed a writ petition in the Madras High Court against the permit cancellation. On 21 November 2015, the Madras High Court granted stay on the Tamil Nadu Registrar of Societies' order cancelling the registration of Greenpeace India.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_Nordic">Greenpeace Nordic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Greenpeace Nordic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_Nordic" title="Greenpeace Nordic">Greenpeace Nordic</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_Nordic" title="Greenpeace Nordic">Greenpeace Nordic</a> is registered in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> with offices also in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>.</p>
<p>Prior to 1998 Greenpeace Nordic was divided into Greenpeace Sweden, Greenpeace Norway, Greenpeace Denmark, and Greenpeace Finland. Because of the unsuccessful anti-whale campaign in Norway in the early 1990s Greenpeace lost all economic support in Norway and they had to close the national branch. In Sweden however Greenpeace had more than 80.000 donators, so they decided to merge all national Nordic Greenpeace organizations into Greenpeace Nordic.<sup id="cite_ref-m.db.no_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m.db.no-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_Switzerland">Greenpeace Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Greenpeace Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Switzerland, the organization is affiliated as "Greenpeace Schweiz" (German) and "Greenpeace Suisse" (French). Founded in 1984, it is a Swiss government recognized NGO.<sup id="cite_ref-greenpeace-ch_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenpeace-ch-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenpeace_USA">Greenpeace USA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Greenpeace USA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_USA" title="Greenpeace USA">Greenpeace USA</a></div>
<p>Greenpeace USA was founded in 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-Greenpeace_History.2C_Chronology.2C_the_Founding_of_Greenpeace_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace_History.2C_Chronology.2C_the_Founding_of_Greenpeace-231">[231]</a></sup> and is one of the largest environmental organizations in the United States. Executive directors of <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_USA" title="Greenpeace USA">Greenpeace USA</a> have included <a href="/wiki/Richard_Grossman_(author)" title="Richard Grossman (author)">Richard Grossman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Dudley" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbara Dudley">Barbara Dudley</a>, Kristin Engberg, John Passacantando, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Radford" title="Phil Radford">Phil Radford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leonard" title="Annie Leonard">Annie Leonard</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenteams_and_Greenwire">Greenteams and Greenwire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenpeace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Greenteams and Greenwire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Greenpeace supports small local groups of youths and children who want to join or found a "Greenteam", by providing them with free info materials and mentoring.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>An online platform for community organizing, Greenwire, has been launched globally and for a number of countries: Belgium, France, UK, India, Netherlands, Russia, Thailand and the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>

<li><cite id="CITEREFOstopowich2002" class="citation">Ostopowich, Melanie (2002), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Hmbci90tNtMC&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;dq=Greenpeace&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true"><i>Greenpeace</i></a>, Weigl Publishers, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-59036-020-6" title="Special:BookSources/1-59036-020-6">1-59036-020-6</a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGreenpeace&amp;rft.aufirst=Melanie&amp;rft.aulast=Ostopowich&amp;rft.btitle=Greenpeace&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DHmbci90tNtMC%26lpg%3DPP1%26dq%3DGreenpeace%26pg%3DPP1%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dtrue&amp;rft.isbn=1-59036-020-6&amp;rft.pub=Weigl+Publishers&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Rex Weyler (2004), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=M1GW445y2n4C&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;dq=Greenpeace%3A%20How%20a%20Group%20of%20Ecologists%2C&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true"><i>Greenpeace: How a Group of Ecologists, Journalists and Visionaries Changed the World</i></a>, Rodale <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1594861064" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1594861064</a></li>
